3. Once the red object starts falling, its trajectory will be influenced by gravity, causing it to accelerate downward.  
4. If the red object falls directly downward and the yellow region is below it, then it will eventually make contact with the yellow region.  
5. However, the position of the red object relative to the yellow region is critical. In this case, the red object is slightly to the left of the yellow region, so it may not fall directly into the yellow region unless there's a horizontal movement or collision that redirects it.  

**Conclusion for Scene A:** It is **possible**, but not guaranteed, due to the red object’s lateral position relative to the yellow region.

---

### **Scene B**

- The green object is moving horizontally toward the red object from the left.

1. The green object is moving horizontally toward the red object, which is directly above the yellow region.

4. If the red object falls straight down due to gravity, it will definitely make contact with the yellow region.
